  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b682678a-037c-4163-85e9-b6707d32b9ea'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer845652095284219406">S@motność w Sieci" - powieść tak współczesna, że bardziej nie można: z Internetem, pagerem, elektronicznymi biletami lotniczymi, dekodowaniem genomu i SMS-ami. A przy tym tak tradycyjna jak klasyczna historia miłosna. Powieść o miłości w Internecie. Tej ostatecznej, tej, o której się marzy, takiej, aby "się popłakać i aby dech zaparło". Wiśniewski analitycznie i urzekająco</span>
  <span id="freeText845652095284219406" style="display:none">S@motność w Sieci" - powieść tak współczesna, że bardziej nie można: z Internetem, pagerem, elektronicznymi biletami lotniczymi, dekodowaniem genomu i SMS-ami. A przy tym tak tradycyjna jak klasyczna historia miłosna. Powieść o miłości w Internecie. Tej ostatecznej, tej, o której się marzy, takiej, aby "się popłakać i aby dech zaparło". Wiśniewski analitycznie i urzekająco zarazem relacjonuje tę miłość, wprowadzając na przemian nastrój nieomal uroczystej czułości, aby kilka linijek dalej zadziwić odważnym erotyzmem. "S@motność w Sieci" to także hołd składany mądrości i wiedzy. Splecione kunsztownie z wątkiem miłosnym fascynujące historie o molekułach emocji, o tym, kto tak naprawdę odkrył DNA, i o tym, co po śmierci stało się z mózgiem Einsteina. Przeczytawszy "S@motność w Sieci", wie się, że wirtualność Internetu to tylko umowa i że e-mail - tak naprawdę - nie musi się różnić od listu przysłanego zaprzęgiem przez posłańca.</span>
  <a data-text-id="845652095284219406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145819999?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=polska-polka">polska-polka</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145819999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16050926374265103741">I read this when it first came out and still remember how goofy it was. It's a love story written by a man(!). But it's not just that. The author is a doctor of economy, IT and physics(!) and has a PHD in chemistry. How educated is that? <br/>Sadly it also speaks volumes about the book, which is one big cliche. It's about two people - a man and a woman - who fall in love by talking on ICQ. The man is an expert in genetic, and the woman is some rich broad who starts to cheat on her husband with this d</span>
  <span id="freeText16050926374265103741" style="display:none">I read this when it first came out and still remember how goofy it was. It's a love story written by a man(!). But it's not just that. The author is a doctor of economy, IT and physics(!) and has a PHD in chemistry. How educated is that? <br />Sadly it also speaks volumes about the book, which is one big cliche. It's about two people - a man and a woman - who fall in love by talking on ICQ. The man is an expert in genetic, and the woman is some rich broad who starts to cheat on her husband with this dude. Since we obviously all have nothing better to do than read the love adventures of two boring people who don't have to work and are so stacked on cash that they're unhappy we might as well give this a shot. FAIL. There are tons of pages related to genetics (which is the profession of the protagonist...and obviously a hobby of the author) and that's pretty much it. The concept is interesting (a long distance relationship) but the two lovers are so mindnumbingly boring. Not just the guy, the woman is even worse. If you think that a man who holds a PHD in everything understands how women think and act - well, let's say you're mistaken. Poorly written erotica is the least of his problems. <br />To sum up - this book is quite an achievement, because it made love sound so completely boring. I only gave it two stars because there's this subplot which involves a beautiful deaf girl, but it too is cliched and mercifully short. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16050926374265103741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/34354652-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/17901415-loneliness-in-the-net">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256767561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16401541097955961580">I usually can read an average length novel in 3-5 days. This one took me so long because the translation into English was terrible.<br/>That is why I rated it 3 stars instead of 4. I Liked the book but struggled with the translation. <br/>I believe it was written around 2001, so what was cutting edge modern living then, seems like ancient history now (dial-up modems, reserving a hotel room online OMG, yikes!)...<br/>In spite of this the author did weave some interesting characters that were shamelessly candid </span>
  <span id="freeText16401541097955961580" style="display:none">I usually can read an average length novel in 3-5 days. This one took me so long because the translation into English was terrible.<br />That is why I rated it 3 stars instead of 4. I Liked the book but struggled with the translation. <br />I believe it was written around 2001, so what was cutting edge modern living then, seems like ancient history now (dial-up modems, reserving a hotel room online OMG, yikes!)...<br />In spite of this the author did weave some interesting characters that were shamelessly candid with each other, owing, I believe, to the anonymity associated with internet/virtual relationships and that still can hold true today. Also illustrated was the ability to love more than one person, albeit differently, simultaneously, as well as love someone today while still not letting go of a love lost from the past. <br />I read books for the character's personalities and their relationships to one another. Often, the plot is secondary or almost irrelevant to me although in this book the premise was believable and more common today than ever. Virtual love, long distance love affairs, unconditional love, love lost, and new love are all touched upon here so overall I liked the book and the author... just find a better translator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16401541097955961580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer977078213987731727">Sometimes I have a feeling that it's not time for me yet to read the book, but then it's like a strike - I feel that I NEED to read it. Just as it happened with this very book "Loneliness on the net". <br/>At the moment, I can say that it is one of my favorite books, maybe not even because it's such a great book, but mostly because I have read it when I had the same situation in my life. I couldn't stop comparing it with the famous book by Glattauer "Love virtually". Actually, "Love virtually" has ev</span>
  <span id="freeText977078213987731727" style="display:none">Sometimes I have a feeling that it's not time for me yet to read the book, but then it's like a strike - I feel that I NEED to read it. Just as it happened with this very book "Loneliness on the net". <br />At the moment, I can say that it is one of my favorite books, maybe not even because it's such a great book, but mostly because I have read it when I had the same situation in my life. I couldn't stop comparing it with the famous book by Glattauer "Love virtually". Actually, "Love virtually" has even it's continuation and the second one has a happy end, which is not very realistic, by the way. "Loneliness..." doesn't have a happy end, which is not very realistic either...everything was so good and then BADABOOM, she's pregnant from another man and they cannot be together. Okay, then...<br />I strongly believe in romantic stories on the Internet, maybe because personally I had a lot of them. And even though they never had a happy end, they weren't so disappointing and depressive either, we have a chance to know people we would probably never know or meet in real life without the help of Internet. And I believe that there can be real love and a veeeeeeeery happy end after all that) </span>

<div id="review_77174662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77174662" />
    <a title="Lucky Suerte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924580-lucky-suerte"><img alt="Lucky Suerte" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77174662?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucky Suerte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucky Suerte" href="/user/show/2924580-lucky-suerte">Lucky Suerte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924580-lucky-suerte?shelf=cliches">cliches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer77174662&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77174662" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12956262990716436152">First of all, either the translation is terrible or the translator has such a nasty streak that he deliberately translated a horribly written work without telling the author. I prefer to believe the former. That being said, it would seem that Wisniewski has never met a cliche he didn't like. From the misunderstood, but brilliant illegitimate child of an American politico and his Latino servant girl, to soulful black jazz players in New Orleans, to the gorgeous, rich woman who makes passionate lo</span>
  <span id="freeText12956262990716436152" style="display:none">First of all, either the translation is terrible or the translator has such a nasty streak that he deliberately translated a horribly written work without telling the author. I prefer to believe the former. That being said, it would seem that Wisniewski has never met a cliche he didn't like. From the misunderstood, but brilliant illegitimate child of an American politico and his Latino servant girl, to soulful black jazz players in New Orleans, to the gorgeous, rich woman who makes passionate love to grand opera, to the dying girl, whom he saves, to his doomed love-affair with a beautiful deaf woman, he's got 'em all. Not only that, he includes bizarre stereotypes, e.g., "An American university might lack a library, but there had to be a pop machine with coke." (He's referring to Princeton here ?!?) There is also a really strange speculation about JFK's sexual fetishes, but I'll leave that to the reader to discover. "Daring eroticism," says the book jacket: "Once he asked the color of the underwear she was wearing that day." Oh, please! At first, I reminded myself that this is a work of fiction, but after viewing Wisniewski's web site, I found myself in prayer: "Lord, help me be the person Wisniewski thinks he is." OK, it's easy to be negative and perhaps it is only because I do sympathize with many of the points he wants to make about the world, life, and particularly "love" on the Internet. This guy really is smart, cultured, etc., but Nabokov he is not! I won't spoil it for you, but Wisniewski does do the decent thing with his character at the end - though it is a bit extreme, given the circumstances. The conclusion is almost realistic, but I did feel like recommending that he just take salsa lessons, or something. Or, better, in the words of that noted American philosopher, Bart Simpson: "Don't have a cow, man." I am glad the real Wisniewski has real, live daughters and is not so "lonely." </span>
  <a data-text-id="12956262990716436152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3692853273519007029" style="display:none">Wiśniewski's bestelling novel had been on my reading list for a long time. I had second thoughts, to be honest, being so popular and on everyone's lips, I wasn't waiting much from it. However, this well-known story about love on the net proved to be rather nice and romantic. Of what I'm absolutely certain is that Wiśniewski's got a special, incomparable talent for writing books about women. He has a profound psychological knowledge of women's nature, their behaviour. If I didn't know the author is a male I would say he's a female, how possibly can he know us women so well? <br />Overall, it's a pretty nice read, makes you think more about the value of realtionships between men and women, all the troubles, barriers and ordeals we are ready to overcome in order to find that very Mr or Mrs Right.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759105088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12834948702439616762">The first book by Wisniewski that I ever read - admittedly, because of the hype. I haven't regretted it a single moment, though, because for me, it completely lived up to expectations. I haven't seen a lot of women write female POV as well as Janusz Leon does it. It's not just about the big things, not even just about the characters' emotions, it's about all the tiny details that make them what they are and keeps their relationship going. Definitely worth reading, just to figure out whether this</span>
  <span id="freeText12834948702439616762" style="display:none">The first book by Wisniewski that I ever read - admittedly, because of the hype. I haven't regretted it a single moment, though, because for me, it completely lived up to expectations. I haven't seen a lot of women write female POV as well as Janusz Leon does it. It's not just about the big things, not even just about the characters' emotions, it's about all the tiny details that make them what they are and keeps their relationship going. Definitely worth reading, just to figure out whether this is "your" writer or not.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RNIoZGtKN1ZV4Je7itWnrsRILKIkmPGJ+njp/CBTtu4YIUvp3bHCBnEUA7THe2HXwx1193b58SHbToL0WQZIIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ITtTezjjHQyOm93YAi3d36E4Z/uOttFIyKFfJPXddGh9yDD2jhjoXKpvSddPgxumpm0+rtzX0eDplzQsjIiKpw==')})
  }
//]]>

The country\'s 24 million people live under a violent dictator<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13340634663115408348\" style=\"display:none\">**Named one of the best books of 2015 by The Economist** Private Markets, Fashion Trends, Prison Camps, Dissenters and Defectors.North Korea is one of the most troubled societies on earth. The country\'s 24 million people live under a violent dictatorship led by a single family, which relentlessly pursues the development of nuclear arms, which periodically incites risky military clashes with the larger, richer, liberal South, and which forces each and every person to play a role in the &quot;theater state&quot; even as it pays little more than lip service to the wellbeing of the overwhelming majority. With this profoundly anachronistic system eventually failed in the 1990s, it triggered a famine that decimated the countryside and obliterated the lives of many hundreds of thousands of people. However, it also changed the lives of those who survived forever. A lawless form of marketization came to replace the iron rice bowl of work in state companies, and the Orwellian mind control of the Korean Workers\' Party was replaced for many by dreams of trade and profit. A new North Korea Society was born from the horrors of the era—one that is more susceptible to outside information than ever before with the advent of k-pop and video-carrying USB sticks. This is the North Korean society that is described in this book. In seven fascinating chapters, the authors explore what life is actually like in modern North Korea today for the ordinary &quot;man and woman on the street.&quot; They interview experts and tap a broad variety of sources to bring a startling new insider\'s view of North Korean society—from members of Pyongyang\'s ruling families to defectors from different periods and regions, to diplomats and NGOs with years of experience in the country, to cross-border traders from neighboring China, and textual accounts appearing in English, Korean and Chinese sources.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/822047.Janusz_Leon_Wi_niewski">About Janusz Leon Wiśniewski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/822047.Janusz_Leon_Wi_niewski"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1557078705p3/822047.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10370504774421096067">Janusz Leon Wiśniewski (ur. 18 sierpnia 1954 w Toruniu) – naukowiec i pisarz polski, magister fizyki (Uniwersytet Mikołaja Kopernika), magister ekonomii (Uniwersytet Mikołaja Kopernika), doktor informatyki (Politechnika Warszawska), doktor habilitowany chemii (Politechnika Łódzka).<br/><br/>Wiśniewski pracował w latach 1979–1987 w Ogólnouczelnianym Ośrodku Obliczeniowym UMK. Na stałe mieszka we Frankfurcie </span>
  <span id="freeText10370504774421096067" style="display:none">Janusz Leon Wiśniewski (ur. 18 sierpnia 1954 w Toruniu) – naukowiec i pisarz polski, magister fizyki (Uniwersytet Mikołaja Kopernika), magister ekonomii (Uniwersytet Mikołaja Kopernika), doktor informatyki (Politechnika Warszawska), doktor habilitowany chemii (Politechnika Łódzka).<br /><br />Wiśniewski pracował w latach 1979–1987 w Ogólnouczelnianym Ośrodku Obliczeniowym UMK. Na stałe mieszka we Frankfurcie nad Menem, gdzie pracuje w międzynarodowej firmie informatycznej zajmującej się tworzeniem oprogramowania dla chemików. Współautor pierwszego w świecie programu komputerowego AutoNom do automatycznego tworzenia systematycznych nazw organicznych związków chemicznych na podstawie ich wzorów strukturalnych. W latach 1999–2007 pracował na stanowisku profesora nadzwyczajnego w Pomorskiej Akademii Pedagogicznej w Słupsku.<br /><br />Ojciec dwóch córek: Joanny i Adrianny.<br /><br />Jako pisarz zadebiutował w roku 2001 powieścią S@motność w Sieci, na podstawie której powstał film oraz serial telewizyjny wyprodukowany przez TVP. Kinowa premiera filmu odbyła się 7 września 2006 roku w Warszawie. Film na nośniku DVD dostępny w Polsce od 5 grudnia 2006 roku.<br /><br />Teatr Baltijskij Dom w St. Petersburgu w Rosji zaadaptował i wystawił spektakl na podstawie S@motności w Sieci (premiera 20 lutego 2009).<br /><br />S@motność w Sieci, Molekuły emocji i Bikini ukazały się w Polsce także w postaci książek mówionych.<br /><br />W 2002 roku wydał Martynę – nowelę napisaną wspólnie z internautami. Książka składa się z trzech opowiadań o losach młodej studentki i grona jej przyjaciół. Początki każdego z opowiadań zostały napisane przez Wiśniewskiego. Stały się punktem wyjścia i inspiracją dla dalszych poczynań tysięcy internautów. Pisarz spośród nadesłanych propozycji wybrał najlepsze jego zdaniem zakończenia. Zostały one dołączone do opowiadania i razem wydane. Pierwszy nakład książki to 35 tysięcy egzemplarzy.<br /><br />Tłumaczenia jego książek jak dotychczas ukazały się w Rosji, Chorwacji, Czechach, na Ukrainie, w Bułgarii, Albanii, Wietnamie i na Litwie.<br /><br />Jest także stałym felietonistą miesięcznika Pani. Książki: Intymna teoria względności, Molekuły emocji i Sceny z życia za ścianą są zbiorami tekstów drukowanych na łamach tego czasopisma. Został uhonorowany w Alei Gwiazd w swym rodzinnym mieście Toruniu (gdzie się uczył i mieszkał) i gdzie na Rynku Staromiejskim odsłonił czwartą z serii "Katarzynek" - podpisów słynnych torunian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10370504774421096067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
